If you die, you lose almost everything. You keep your fame, your gold (premium currency), your pet, and everything in your vault, but lose everything else.\n\nWhen you start, you\'ll have nothing. You go into the game, start killing enemies, picking up some low-tier items and everything is good. As you walk further away from spawn, the enemies start getting tougher and drop better items. Eventually, you\'ll end up in a place called the "godlands" which is located somewhere around the center of the map, where you can kill gods for the higher tier items, stat potions, and eggs. I\'ll talk about the eggs and stat potions for a bit, since they\'re both important.\n\nStat potions are the main trading currency in the game, and the game is big on trading, so stat pots are very valuable to find. (You can look up what they each do on the wiki.)\n\nPets are HUGE in this game! There are several families of pets (avian, feline, canine, farm, etc.) and each have different skins for each rarity. things you can't use, which unfortunately can't be recycled or used in any way (see the microtansactions point which brings that up)\n\nProgression-The game feels like a rogue lite Gauntlet as it's primary gameplay elments, despite having permadeath in the context of you have to restart at level 1 rankwsie when you start a new run, this adds challenge and replayability because the game does let you keep class unlocks and your progress towards unlocking new characters, which is nice and makes the game feel less grindy\n\nSimplicity and Feel-The game is simple enough to understand, but can be hard to play at times in terms of getting overwhelmed, which is the nature of Gauntlet esqe style games, and you will enjoy trying to hoard resources mowing enemies down whilst trying to survive as long as you can and completing as many quests as possible \n\nAs a note, think of the quests as a very basic but effective approach to Skyrim's quests, just go to where a boss is, and take it out, but as brought up before, this is the only quest type you can do, which is mildly dissapointing\n\nOverall Realm of the Mad God is a fun game, but don't expect it to be a big hit or a great revolutionary cost you anything provided you act smart when you try the game out and don't buy anything, also, to some it may seem like it's problems are too hindering and make it a chore to play, while others will
